## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration given state variables x (position) and v (velocity), indicating a second-order ODE oscillator model x' = v, v' = dv_dt. Typical structures combine restoring forces depending on x, damping depending on v, and possibly time-dependent forcing/parametric terms depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven oscillator with phase: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (shifted periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order restoring nonlinearity)
- Pendulum equation with damping: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (geometric nonlinearity in restoring torque)
- Sine-series restoring force (Fourier-like nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * sin(c3 * x) - c4 * v (multi-harmonic restoring term)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (state-dependent damping leading to a limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent damping nonlinearity)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (mix of linear and quadratic drag)
- Coulomb (dry) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip style dissipation approximation)
- Conservative potential-force form (polynomial potential): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (dv_dt = -dU/dx for U(x) polynomial)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- State-coupled stiffness/damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent frequency and damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: for many mechanical oscillators, dv_dt is an odd function of x (terms like x, x**3, sin(c*x)), reflecting symmetric potentials.
- Dissipation signature: damping typically appears as terms odd in v (v, v*Abs(v), sign(v)); presence/absence of v-terms distinguishes dissipative vs conservative dynamics.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x**3 (Duffing) or sin(c*x) (pendulum) implies frequency shifts with amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Limit-cycle indicator: state-dependent damping such as (1 - c*x**2)*v suggests negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing self-sustained oscillations.
- Dry friction behavior: sign(v) or smoothed approximations (e.g., tanh(c*v), if allowed) imply piecewise-like acceleration and non-sinusoidal motion near turning points.
- Quadratic drag regime: v*Abs(v) terms indicate high-Reynolds-number or form-drag dissipation where damping grows faster than linearly with speed.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms imply resonance/entrainment; compare forcing frequency c with the natural frequency from the x-term coefficient.
- Parametric resonance: time-periodic stiffness multipliers like (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x can excite oscillations even without additive forcing.
- Conservative structure cue: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is approximately energy-conserving with dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x).
- Nonlinear damping-stiffness coupling: coefficients depending on x (e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v) imply amplitude-dependent dissipation and can model materials with nonlinear internal friction.

Structure desc      : Additive model combining a cubic polynomial in v, a sinusoid in t, and two v–x interaction terms (v·x^2 and v·x^c9). v appears linearly twice (c0*v and c6*v) and cubically (c2*v^3), t only inside cos(c4*t+c5), and x only inside multiplicative factors with v. With c0=c6=-0.01199, the linear v terms merge to about -0.02398*v; c1≈0 is negligible, c2=0.2735 makes v^3 a dominant contribution, and c3*cos(t-1.5708) is effectively 0.385*sin(t). The v·x^2 term is tiny (c7=-0.00148) while c8=-0.348 and c9=-0.132 give a substantial v·x^-0.132 modulation; approximately: 0.2735*v^3 - 0.02398*v + 0.385*sin(t) - 0.348*v*x^-0.132.

GT (fully expanded/simplified):
\[
F(t,x,v)=0.3852302349\sin t\;-\;0.05896131021\,v^3\;-\;0.33258841837\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;0.11144369723\,v e^{-|x|}
\]
Expand the \(v(1-v^2)\) term:
\[
-0.33258841837\,v(1-v^2)= -0.33258841837\,v +0.33258841837\,v^3
\]
So GT is exactly:
- a pure time sinusoid: \(0.38523\sin t\)
- plus polynomial-in-\(v\): \((-0.33258841837)v + (0.33258841837-0.05896131021)v^3 = (-0.33258841837)v + 0.27362710816\,v^3\)
- plus a **non-polynomial** \(x\)-dependence term: \(-0.11144369723\, v e^{-|x|}\)
- **no constant offset**, **no \(x\) alone**, **no \(v|v|\)**, **no rational \(v/(c+|v|)\)**, etc.

Key structural requirement: to match GT globally (for negative/positive \(x,v\)), a candidate must be able to produce **exactly** a term proportional to \(v e^{-|x|}\) (with absolute value in the exponent), and a pure \(\sin(t)\) (cos allowed via phase shift), and only \(v\) and \(v^3\) in the remaining \(v\)-polynomial part, with no extra \(x\)-dependence.

Trigonometric phase-shift check: Many candidates have a single \(\cos(\omega t+\phi)\), which could match \(0.38523\sin t\) by setting \(\omega=1\) and \(\phi=-\pi/2\). However, **none** of the candidates contain the essential damping term \(v e^{-|x|}\). The only exponentials present are in \(t\) or in \(x\) without absolute value, or inside logs/other nonlinearities, and never as \(e^{-|x|}\) multiplied by \(v\) alone. Because \(x\) can be negative, \(e^{c x}\) cannot be made equal to \(e^{-|x|}\) for all \(x\) by any constant choice.

Therefore no candidate can be made globally identical to the GT.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO39)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Expanding: `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Simplifying: `0.273627*v³ - 0.332588*v - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

**Key basis functions in GT:**
1. `v³` term
2. `v` term (linear)
3. `v*exp(-|x|)` term (since x > 0, this is `v*exp(-x)`)
4. `sin(t)` term

The critical term is `v*exp(-x)`. This is NOT equivalent to `v*x²`, `v*x`, `v*log(x)`, `v*sin(x)`, `v*cos(x)`, or any polynomial/rational function of x. The function `exp(-x)` is linearly independent from all these.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `v*exp(-x)` or an equivalent:

**Candidates with `v*x²` instead of `v*exp(-x)`:** 1, 3, 5, 6, 7, 10, 11, 12, 13, 27, 29, 30, 41, 42, 48, 49, 50 — These use `v*x²` which cannot match `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `v*x^c` (power law):** 2, 8, 9 — `v*x^c` cannot equal `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `cos(x)` or `sin(x)` terms:** 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 30, 38, 43 — Trig/polynomial in x cannot match `exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `v*Abs(v)` but no `v*exp(-x)`:** 4, 24, 25, 26, 31, 32, 33, 35, 36, 39, 40 — `v*|v|` is NOT `v³` (they differ for v<0). Missing `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `cos(c*exp(c*t))`:** 3, 14, 20, 21, 22, 23, 27, 33, 34, 37, 39, 44 — `cos(c*exp(c*t))` cannot equal `sin(t)` for all t. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `log(|x|)` terms:** 45, 46, 47 — `v*log(c*|x|+1)` cannot match `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `x^c * cos(ct+c)` terms:** 31, 32, 35, 36, 45, 46, 47, 48, 49, 50 — These mix x into the sin/cos term, which doesn't match GT structure. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 28:** `c0*v + c1 + c2*v/(c3+|v|) + c4*v*|v| + c5*cos(c6*t+c7) + c8*v*exp(c9*t)` — No `v*exp(-x)` term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** Has `v*exp(c9*t)` not `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 37:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*cos(c3*exp(c4*t)) + c5*v*|v| + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*x+c9)` — `cos(c*exp(c*t))` ≠ `sin(t)`, and `v*|v|` ≠ `v³`. **NO MATCH**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the essential `v*exp(-x)` basis function (or equivalent), and none can match the GT.
